BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK COUNTY
COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

COOK COUNTY INMATE PROCESSING FEE ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the Cook County Sheriffs Office processes inmates entering and exiting from the Cook
County Jail, expending a great deal of manpower and resources to accomplish this task; and

3172

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 2001

WHEREAS, the Cook County Sheriff desires to establish a fee for processing inmates, except in cases
where the inmate is indigent; and
WHEREAS, Section 730 ILCS 125/20 allows the County Board to require convicted persons confined in
the County Jail to reimburse the County for the costs of the convicted person' s incarceration.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County:
Sections:
I.
2.
3.
4.
5.
6.

Amount
Collection
Notice
Severability
Short Title
Effective Date

Section 1. Amount
That the Cook County Sheriff shall assess a processing fee of $25.00 for each inmate, to be
charged after conviction, if that inmate was or will be housed within any of Cook County's
jails.

Section 2. Collection
That the processing fee shall be collected upon conviction of the inmate or the fee shall be
deducted from the inmate's Trust Account and deposited in the Cook County General Fund to
be appropriated pursuant to Illinois Law.

Section 3. Notice
Upon entering any County jail an inmate shall be informed, by signs or other written
documents, of the fee the inmate must pay upon conviction.

Section 4. Severablity
If any portion of this Ordinance or the application therefore to any person or circumstance is
held invalid, such invalidity does not affect other provisions or applications of this Ordinance
which can be given effect without the invalid application or provision, and to this end the
provisions of this Ordinance are declared to be severable. If any section, sentence or clause
of this Ordinance shall be adjudged unconstitutional, such adjudication shall not affect the
validity of the Ordinance as a whole or of any section, sentence or clause thereof not
adjudged unconstitutional.

Section 5. Short Title
This Ordinance shall be known and may be cited as the Cook County Inmate Processing Fee
Ordinance.

Section 6. Effective Date
This Ordinance shall be effective December I, 200 I.

3173

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 200 I

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Moran moved that the Proposed Ordinance be referred to the Comm ittee on Finance. The
motion died for lack of a second.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, on September I I, 200 I, the United States of America was shocked by an attack within our
borders; and
WHEREAS, by Joint Resolution, the Congress of the Un ited States of America committed to support
increased resources in the war to eradicate terrorism ; and
WHEREAS, the tragic events of September 11th caused the Federal Government and Governments
around th e world to consider and increase security efforts; and
WHEREAS, the American public supports increased sec urity in order to protect our nation, American
citi zens and others in our Country; and
WHEREAS, buildings in and around C hicago have increased the security presence and actions around
their bui ldings; and
WHEREAS, access to the Daley Plaza and Courtrooms in the pedway requires search by Sheriffs
Officers, with metal detectors and scanning bags and packages; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Sheriff's Officers and Chicago Police Department have increased the
number of officers in and around the County Building, City Hall and Daley Plaza; and
WHEREAS, although the current security can protect the area and the people in and around the County
Building, City Hall and pedway from harm, other security measures should be examined.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
Cook County Sheriffs Department s hould examine security here at and around the County Building in
order to protect everyone in and near the County Building.

This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsor.

CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Chicago Systems Group,
Inc. (CSG), Chicago, Illinois, to provide several critical enhancements and improvements to the Traffic
Rewrite Information Management System (TRIMS) used in the Traffic Division of the Circuit Court.

3 177

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 200 I

Reason:

Chicago Systems Group, Inc. began its involvement with the Traffic System in October 1998
and early in 1999 took over management of the project. CSG's understanding of the system,
operational procedures, and environmental constraints of the TRIMS system are unique. CSG
will provide the following enhancements to the TRIMS system: cash register connectivity,
the capture of townsh ip road information, the design for the implementation of Supreme
Court Rule 529, and creation of Warrants and Failure to Pay form s. ADC, Chicago, Ill inois,
will provide Minority Business Enterprise/Women Minority Enterprise participation in this
contract.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $219,600.00 [$175 ,000.00 - (348-260 Account); and $44,600.00 - (358-260
Account)]. Contract period: October I, 200 I through January 3 1, 2002. Requisition Nos. 13480675 and
13580653.
T he Chief Information Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to ente r into the requested contract. The motion carried.

Commissioner Moran voted " present".

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY CLERK
CONTRACTS

Transmitting a Communication from
DAVID OR R, County Clerk
by
GARY RYCYZYN, Director of Elections
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Cook County Suburban
Publishers, Inc., Chicago, Illinois, for publications for the two (2) elections to be held in 2002 .
Reason:

Pursuant to statute, election notices are required to be published in one or more newspapers
published in each political subdivision having general circulation in the subdivision. Cook
County Suburban Publishers, Inc. is the only company who can provide the Election
Department with this type of service needed to comply with the statutory deadlines for each
notice. Cook County Suburban Publ ishers, Inc. assembles the notice, dispatches to each local
publisher and supplies the Election Department with camera-ready copies of each notice
needed for publication in a County-wide newspaper.

Estimated Fiscal Impact:
25240007.

$600,000.00. One time purchase.

(524-245 Account).

BUREAU OF INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY AND AUTOMATION
CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
CATHERINE MARAS O' LEARY, Chief lnfonnation Officer,
Bureau of Information Technology & Automation
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with ASAP Software, Buffalo
Grove, Illinois, for a County-wide Microsoft software and software support services agreement.
Reason:

Microsoft does not sell its products directly to consumers. ASAP Software is an authorized
large accou nt reseller of Microsoft products and was the successful bidder, winning the State
of Illinois contract for Microsoft products. Because of the substantial volume of Microsoft
products purchased by the State through ASAP Software, the State receives Microsoft's
highest available discount of up to 50% on software and software support services. The Chief
Information Officer will reduce the amount spent on the 200 I County-wide computer contract
by $ 1,292,691.41, transferring that amount to this contract to purchase Microsoft products
from ASAP Software. The net fi scal impact of this request, therefore, is no increase in
spending, but rather a more efficient use of dollars already allocated.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $1 ,292,691.4 1. One time purchase. (717/various-579 Accounts). Requisition
No. 1009001 3.
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

Comm issioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the request of the Chief
lnfonnation Officer be approved, as amended and that the County Purchasing Agent be authorized to
enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT
HOME INVESTMENT PARTNERSHIPS PROGRAM
Trans mitting a Communication, dated August 21 , 200 I from
GWENDOLYN D. CLEMONS, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re: HOME Investment Partnerships Program (HOM E Program)
respectfully request approval of $ 1,000,000.00 in Home Investment Partnerships Program matching funds
to be used for the rehabilitation of approximately 20 single-family homes fo r low- and very-low income
households in s uburban Cook County. HOM E Program contracts will be executed between regional or
area agencies and the County of Cook. Approval of th is loan will enable Cook County to contin ue the
Owner-occupied Single-family Rehabilitation Program in unincorporated Cook or vill ages that do not
administer rehab programs.
The project complies with the HOME Program regulations and furthers the goals of the Five-Year
Consol idated Community Development Plan (approved by U.S. Department of Housing and Urban
Development on October 17, 2000).
Permanent liens are placed on the properties for the amount of the rehabilitation by the participating
agency. After rehabilitation is completed, the agency w ill then assign the Note, Owner's Participation
Agreement, and Junior Mortgage to Cook County. The Cook County Home Program w ill recapture funds
expended on the projects when these homes are sold, transferred, or otherwise alienated and title is
transferred.

32 10

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 200 1
Respectfully request approval of this proposed use of HOME funds, and that the Chief Admini strative
Officer of the County of Cook, or his designee, be authorized to execute on behalf of the County of Cook
any and all documents necessary to further the project approved herein, including but not limited to
Subgrantee Agreements, Intergovernmental Agreements, amendments and modifications thereto, loan
documents, lien assignments, releases of mortgages and liens, and mortgage assumptions.
Fiscal Impact: $ 1,000,000.00. (772-292 Account).
Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Carr, moved that the request of the Director of the
Department of Planning and Development be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

VILLAGE OF GLENWOOD
NO CASH BID REQUEST
Transmitting a Communication, dated September 18, 200 I from
DEBORAH SIMS, Chairman, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee
Submitting a request from
BRUCE M. BUYER, Buyer and Ruben, Attorney at Law
Re:

No Cash Bid Application
Permanent Index Number 32-03-328-012-0000

3230

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 2001

We represent the Village of Glenwood relative to this Application. The purpose of this letter is to advise
you of the Village's desire to continue its participation in the Cook County No Cash Bid Program. It is
interested in acquiring the following parcel in its comm unity that has been delinquent in real estate taxes
for two or more years, pursuant to 35 I LCS 200/2 1-90. The years available for purchase for Permanent
Index Number 32-03 -328-0 I 2-0000 are I 984 through 1999, inclusive. Please accept this request to obtain
said property which is also listed on the submitted Exhibit "A". Said parcel is located in Glenwood,
Illinois.
The above parcel is adjacent to Village owned property and will have a possible future use as an
additional entrance to that property. This parcel is located on Main Street in the heart of Glenwood and is
less than a half block from the new Village Hall complex. Part of the property is located in the flood
plain and would be prohibitive to the construction of any buildings. Since it is in the heart of Glenwood,
the Village will be able to maintain the property for the benefit of all its citizens. THERE ARE NO
TH IRD PARTY APPLICANTS.
In conjunction with the above request, submitted are two original certified copies of Resolutions for each
of the two parcels authorizing their acquisition; copies of Sidwell maps; photographs of the parcel;
Chicago Title Insurance Company Commitment for Title Insurance for said permanent index number
setting forth the information that would normally be contained on tract, tax, and judgment searches.

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Sims, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the communication be referred to the
Comm ittee on Finance Tax Delinquency Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 246429). The motion carried
unanimously.

245585

AN ORDINANCE OF THE COUNTY OF COOK, ILLINOIS APPROVING EXECUTION
OF A TAX REIMBURSEMENT PAYMENT AGREEMENT WITH THE BOEING
COMPANY (PROPOSED ORDINANCE). Transmitting a Communication, dated August 8,
200 I from John H. Stroger, Jr., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners:
The followi ng is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:

3252

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 200 I

PROPOSED ORDINANCE

AN ORDINANCE OF THE COUNTY OF COOK, ILLINOIS
APPROVING EXECUTION OF A
TAX RE IMBURSEMENT PAYMENT AGREEMENT
WITH THE BOEING COMPANY
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Corporate Headquarters Relocation Act, (PA 92-0207), signed into
law on August I, 200 I, as amended from time to time (the "Relocation Act"), the General Assembly of
the State of lllinois (the " State") has determined that the relocation of the international headquarters of
large, multinational corporations from outside of the State to a location within the State creates a
substantial public benefit and will foster economic growth and development; and
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK COUNTY:
SECTION 1. The President of the Board of Commissioners authorized, negotiate, execute and
deliver the Agreement between the County and Boeing in s ubstantially in the form submitted herewith as
Exhibit A and made a part hereof, and such other supporting documents as may be necessary to carry out
and comply with the provisions of the Agreement, with such changes, deletions and insertions as shall be
approved by the persons executing such agreement.
SECTION 2. The annual reimbursement payments required to be made by the County pursuant
to the Agreement may be made without annual appropriation, as provided for under Section 18-1 65(a)(8)
of the Property Tax Code, 35 ILCS 200/ l 8- I 65(a)(8), as the same may be amended.
SECTION 3. The President and County C lerk are authorized to execute and deliver on behalf of
the C ity such other documents, agreements and certificates and to do such other things consistent with the
terms of this Ordinance as such officers and employees shall deem necessary or appropriate in order to
effectuate the intent and purposes of this Ordinance.
SECTION 4. If any provision of this Ordinance shall be held to be invalid or unenforceable for
any reason, the invalidity or unenforceability of s uch provision shall not affect any of the other provisions
of this Ordinance.
SECTION 5. All ordinances, resolutions, motions or orders in conflict with this Ordinance are
hereby repealed to the extent of such conflict.
SECTION 6. This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect immediately upon its passage.
*Referred to the Committee on Finance August 9, 2001.
Chairman Daley asked Robert Kunze, Deputy Commissioner, Department of Planning and Development,
City of Chicago, to address the committee on the Boeing Company item.
Mr. Kunze stated that the Boeing Company recently moved into its new international headquarters at I 00
North Riverside Plaza in Chicago, where its management team will create and coordinate business
strategies. He said Boeing is the world ' s largest aerospace company that has annual revenues of $51
billion, and the location to Chicago was a major and important achievement for the State of Illinois. He
stated the C ity of C hicago is offering to reimburse Boeing's share of real estate taxes for its headquarters
over a period of 20 years. The C ity of Chicago has authority to do this through the recently adopted State
Corporate Headquarters Relocation Act. He indicated that Chicago passed legislation under which the

3253

 JO URNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 200 I

City will re imburse Boeing for the portion of taxes going to the Chicago Public Schools and the City of
Chicago, that is about 73% of the taxes that Boeing will pay. The City is asking the C hicago Park
District, communi ty colleges, Metropolitan Water Reclamation District and Cook County to rebate their
taxes to Boeing. Mr. Kunze said this is an unprecedented request for the City of Chicago, but the request
would not be made unless there were substantial economic benefits to the region. Estimates of the total
economic benefits to the Chicago area are $4.3 billion with approximately $3 to $4 billion to be within
suburban Cook County. Mr. Kunze continued to explain that some of the taxes will come back to the
county in some form of tax revenues from new workers and residences.
Mr. Kunze indicated that the County's investment wi ll be protected since Boeing must maintain its
corporate headquarters in Chicago in order to receive the reimbursement and must maintain 500 jobs in
C hicago. He noted if the jobs fall below 500 but above 400, there is a pro-rated reduction in taxes. In
addition, he noted if the number of j obs falls below 400 in the city, and Boeing is unable to rectify this
during the first ten years, Boeing would have to pay all its reimbursement. He noted that Boeing will
have a corporate benefits program and has agreed to compl y with the City's MBE/ WBE requirements in
the renovation of their offices, which is over $50 million.
Commissioner Lechowicz thought that the residual effects of Boeing' s move would be greater than $4.3
billion. He asked Thomas Glaser, Chief Financial Officer, what would be the fi scal impact on Cook
County?
C hairman Daley noted, for the record, that representati ves of Boeing had planned to attend the meeting,
but are not present due to flights being cancelled.
Mr. Glaser replied that it is anticipated that the County will be rebating taxes that would approximate
$230,000 in year one, and over the 20 year period, the amount would increase to about $330,000. He said
it is expected that the County would assume the Forest Preserve District share of the property tax rebate,
which would be $25,000 this year to $35,000 in year twenty.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked ifthe County' s growth is great enough to absorb this kind of impact?
Mr. Glaser responded in the affirmative and indicated that the direct and indi rect incremental benefits
would help on the revenue side.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked if Mr. Glaser had any projections of growth in this area?
Mr. Glaser answered the total county benefits are $2.8 billion over a 20 year period.
Commissioner Lechowicz requested a detailed statement on the benefici al impacts to Cook County.
Commiss ioner Collins recognized the project and its financial benefits to the County. She stated that
more definitive data is needed before a vote is taken.
C hairman Daley stated that since thi s item was referred to committee on August 9, 200 I, representatives
from the President's staff have been available to respond to questions from commissioners. He stated it is
necessary to vote on this matter today.
Commissioner Collins inquired what will next year' s fiscal impact be and how w ill the deficit be
rectified?

3254

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 200 1

Mr. Glaser responded that the County would find the ability to appropriate next year' s tax payment
through current revenues.
Commissioner Collins asked ifthe amount rebated inc ludes the amount for the Forest Preserve as well?
Mr. Glaser stated that it would be included.
Commissioner Silvestri indicated the Boeing relocation would benefit the City, County, suburbs and
regional counties. He stated it is an important step that could result in more Boeing employees moving to
this region and providing more jobs. The Commissioner said this could be the first wave of other
corporate relocations to the city.
Commissioner Moran expressed initial opposition to the ordinance, but concluded by stating hi s support
and noting that the County should look fo r economic deve lopment in the southern suburbs.
President Stroger stated that financially, this is a good deal and its impact will be inconsequential.
Commissioner Moreno indicated that this project is economic development at its best. It wi ll cost the
County less than I% while the benefits wi ll be in excess of $2.5 billion over 20 years. Boeing anticipates
spending approximately $50 million for the build-out and construction through the use of minority
business enterprises and women business enterprises. When one looks at the Illinois Corporate
Headquarters Relocation Act and its intentions, this is a win-win situation. Commissioner Moreno asked
if Boeing would actively pursue job recruitment of minorities from different levels at the corporate
headquarters?
David Reifman, Attorney for Boeing, Piper, Marbury, Rudnick and Wolfe, answered the Boeing
Company held a successful job fair in Chicago before the corporate relocation and received 7000
applications from throughout the region. One of the reasons Boeing moved to Chicago was to have
access to a diverse community as it seeks to enhance its global image. He concluded by saying that there
is an agreement to maintain a certain number of jobs, and employees will come from everywhere
throughout Cook County and the State of Illinois.
Commissioner Sutker asked Mr. Kunze to explain the 73% reimbursement?
Mr. Kunze noted that 73% of Boeing' s taxes will be rebated by the City of Chicago. The other 27% will
be rebated by the other taxing districts includ ing Cook County, community colleges, the Chicago Park
District and the Metropolitan Water Reclamation. He said Boeing would not want an incentive package
that would harm schools. For clarification purposes, Mr. Kunze stated the schools will not be directly or
indirectly affected by this proposal.
Commissioner Schumann is glad to see that the County is a part of this incentive package and noted it is a
very small amount of money compared to the projected benefits and regional significance.
Vice-Chairman Carr spoke in favor of the item and commented on Tax Increment Financing (TIF). He
noted that Cicero is the largest TIF district producer in tenns of returns coming back in the State of
Illinois. He said economic development is a slow process that involves risk.
Chairman Daley stated the relocation of Boeing is a great day for the City of Chicago and Cook County.
This was brought forth as a result of the leadership of President Stroger, Mayor Daley and Governor
Ryan. He thanked the Boeing Company for locating to Chicago and said he looks forwa rd to working
with the company.

3255

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 2001

Commissioner Lechowicz asked the State's Attorney's Office to address whether the County has the legal
authority to approve Boeing's req uest.
In response to Commissioner Lechow icz's question, Patrick Driscoll, Deputy State's Attorney, stated that
the proposed ordinance follows the State statute. He said Boeing has met all the conditions by volume of
business a nd the like to meet the State requirements. He concluded by saying that the ordinance, on its
face, appears to be valid. He noted that the State's Attorney's Office is not aware of any potential
challenges to the ordinance should it pass. (A letter from the Office of the State's Attorney regarding the
legal a uthority of the Board to enter into this Agreement is on file in the Office of the County Clerk).

Commissioner Lechowicz, seconded by Vice Chairman Carr, moved that the Ordinance
(Communication No. 245585) be approved and adopted. Commissioner Lechowicz called for a Roll
Call, the vote of yeas and nays being as follows:

01-0-26
ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE OF THE COUNTY OF COOK, ILLINOIS
APPROVING EXECUTION OF A
TAX REIMBURSEMENT PAYMENT AGREEMENT
WITH THE BOEING COMPANY
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Corporate Headquarters Relocation Act, ( PA 92-0207), signed into
Jaw on August I , 200 I, as amended from time to time (the "Relocation Act"), the General Assembly of
the State of Illinois (the " State") has determined that the relocation of the internationa l headquarters of
large, multinational corporations from outs ide of the State to a location within the State creates a
substantial public benefit and will foster economic growth and development; and
WHEREAS, the Relocation Act therefore provides for the creation o f certain financial
incentives that may be used to encourage long-tenn commitments by an Eligible Business relocating its
Corporate Headquarters (as such terms are defined in the Relocation Act) in the State; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook (the "Countv"), as an affected taxing district, is authori zed
under the provisions of Section I 8 of the Property Tax Code, 35 ILCS 200/1 et seq., as amended from
time to time (the "Propertv Tax Code"), to, by a majority vote of its governing body, after the
determination of the assessed valuation of its property, to order the Clerk of Cook County to abate any
portion of its taxes on certain types of rea l property. Purs uant to Section I 8-1 65(a)(8) of the Property Tax
Code, 35 ILCS 200/ 18- I 65(a)(8), such abatement may be made with respect to any property or a portion
of any property within the County that is used by an Eligible Business fo r a Corporate Headquarters.
Alternatively, in lieu of such abatement, the County may enter into an agreement with an Eligi ble
Business to make annual payments to such Eligible Business in an amount not to exceed the property
taxes paid directly or indirectly by such Eligible Business to the taxing district and a ny other affected
taxing district(s) for premises occupied purs uant to a written lease and may make such payments without
the need for an annual appropriation. Any s uch abatement or agreement may be effecti ve for the entire
term specified by the County, provided, however, that such abatement or annual payments in lieu thereof
may not exceed 20 years; and
WHEREAS, the Boeing Company (" Boeing") is a large, multinational corporation with worldwide revenues in excess of $50,000,000,000 that presently maintains its international headquarters in
Seattle, Washington. Boeing intends to relocate its international headquarters to the real property
commonly known as I 00 N. Rivers ide Plaza, Chicago, Illinois 60606 (the " Property"'). Jn connection with
such relocation, Boeing has executed that certain Office Lease dated May I 0, 200 I by and between I 00
North Riverside, LLC, as landlord, and Boeing, as tenant (the "Boeing Lease"), pursuant to which Boeing
shall, among other matters, initially lease approximately 275,000 rentable square feet of space including
the top 12 floors of the building located on the Property (the " Building") for an initial period of fifteen
( 15) years, subject to the terms and conditions contained therein. Upon such re location, and during the
Term of the Agreement, as defined in the Tax Reimbursement Pay ment Agreement (the " Agreement")
subm itted hereto as Exhibit A, the portion of the Building occupied by Boeing wi ll be the princi pal office
of Boeing and the site which Boeing's principal executive officers have designated as the ir principal
offices. In connection with its occupancy of the Building, Boeing shall construct substantial tenant
im provements necessary to permit Boeing to take possession in accordance with the terms of the Boeing
Lease. Such relocation wi ll create a s ubstantial public benefit through its creation of not less than 500
permanent FTE jobs (as defined in the Agreement), through Boeing ' s pay ment of various taxes and
governmental charges and through other public benefits described in this Agreement and will also foster
fu rther economic growth and development in the County and State. Therefore, Boeing constitutes an

3257

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 2001

Eligible Business under the Relocation Act and the portion of the Building occupied by Boeing will, upon
such occupancy, constitute Boeing's new Corporate Headquarters; and

WHEREAS, the County's annual reimbursement payments under the Agreement will consist of
the County's allocable share of the Boeing General Real Estate Taxes (as defined in the Agreement), the
Forest Preserve District of Cook County allocable share of the Boeing General Real Estates Taxes, based
on the respective tax rates of such taxing district(s) or fund; and
WHEREAS, the County's agreement to provide the annual reimbursement payments provided
for in the Agreement is conditioned upon, among other things, (i) Boeing's relocation to the Building, as
described above, (ii) Boeing's construction of certain initial Boeing improvements, (iii) Boeing' s
continued status during the Term of the Agreement as an Eligible Business under the Relocation Act, (iv)
the continued status of the portion of the Building occupied by Boeing as a Corporate Headquarters under
the Relocation Act during the Term of the Agreement, (v) Boeing' s relocation to and retention at the
Building of not less than the minimum number of FTE jobs and the corporate headquarters employees
specified in the Agreement during the Term of the Agreement, (vi) Boeing' s lease and occupancy of not
less than the minimum number of square feet at the Building specified in the Agreement during the Term
of the Agreement, and (vii) Boeing's compliance with the job readiness training and public benefit
requirements specified in the Agreement, all subject to the terms and conditions set forth in the
Agreement; and
WHEREAS, Boeing's relocation to the County would not reasonably be anticipated without the
payment of the annual reimbursement payments provided for in the Agreement and the comparable
agreements being executed and delivered by the other taxing districts levying property taxes on the
Property and the Building; now therefore,
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK COUNTY:
SECTION 1. The President of the Board of Commissioners authorized, negotiate, execute and
deliver the Agreement between the County and Boeing substantially in the form submitted hereto as
Exhibit A and made a part hereof, and such other supporting documents as may be necessary to carry out
and comply with the provisions of the Agreement, with s uch changes, deletions and insertions as shall be
approved by the persons executing such agreement.
SECTION 2. The annual reimbursement payments required to be made by the County pursuant
to the Agreement may be made without annual appropriation, as provided for under Section l 8- l 65(a)(8)
of the Property Tax Code, 35 lLCS 200/ l 8-l 65(a)(8), as the same may be amended.
SECTION 3. The Pres ident and County C lerk are authorized to execute and deli ver on behalf of
the City such other documents, agreements and certificates and to do s uch other things consistent with the
terms of this Ordinance as such officers and employees shall deem necessary or appropriate in order to
effectuate the intent and purposes of this Ordinance.
SECTION 4. If any provision of this Ordinance shall be held to be invalid or unenforceable for
any reason, the invalidity or unenforceability of such provision shall not affect any of the other provisions
of this Ordinance.
SECTION 5. All ordinances, resolutions, motions or orders in conflict with this Ordinance are
hereby repealed to the extent of such conflict.
SECTION 6. This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect immediately upon its passage.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 2001

Approved and adopted this 20th day of September 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

transmitting a Communication:

SUBURBAN COUNCIL ON ALCOHOLISM AND SUBSTANCE ABUSE, East Hazel
Crest, Illinois, for treatment of participants in the Drug Treatment Program at the Sixth
Municipal District, Markham, Illinois.
Reason:

This contract will provide substance abuse testing and treatment for nonviolent
adult probationers that have been accepted in the court's Drug Treatment
Programs. Defendants are provided treatment in lieu of incarceration to help
them  confront their addictions and avoid future criminal activities. South
Suburban Council on Alcoholism and Substance Abuse has been providing these
services to the court since 1998. The council was originally selected based upon
its expertise in drug intervention services and the location of its service site.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $150,000.00. Contract period: October 1, 200 I through September
30, 2002. (532-272 Account). Requisition No. 15324029.

246132

CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY, by Henry A. Budzinski, Interim Chief Judge,
transmitting a Communication:
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with TREATMENT
ALTERNATIVES FOR SAFE COMMUNITIES INC. (TASC), Chicago, Illinois, to provide
screening, assessment and diagnostic services and substance abuse testing for minors in the
Juvenile Court Drug Treatment Program for a fourteen month period.
Reason:

The Circuit Court of Cook County initiated this unique program in October 1996
for minors with drug-related offenses who have been identified by the Juvenile
Probation and Court Services Department to be in need of intervention, treatment
services and supervision. The program targets nonviolent delinquent minors
residing in and around the Austin and Lawndale communities in Chicago. The
objective of the program is to provide a continuum of services to these minors to
help them break the cycle of drug dependency. Program services include
substance abuse assessment and treatment, health care, counseling, education,
vocational training and housing placements. Services are provided within a
framework of sanctions and substance abuse testing.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $86,956.00 $74,500.00 (Year 200 I: $12,500.00; and Year 2002:
$74 ,456.00 $62,000.00). Contract period: October I, 2001 through September 30, 2002.
(326-249 Account). Requisition Nos. 13260040 and 23260002.

Chairman Daley stated that the President' s Office as well as other commissioners have asked to have
these offices meet to determine if there is any duplication of services.
Jim Anderson, Director of Financial Control, Office of the Chief Judge, stated that his office will
cooperate in the study.
Commissioner Silvestri asked how long these programs have been in existence and inq uired as to the
success of the programs in terms of recidivism?
Mr. Anderson stated the juvenile programs started in 1995 and the adult program began in 1998, all of
which have been extraordinary in the ir success. The Juvenile Drug Program has seen about a 60%
success rate where juveniles are off drugs and back in school. The Evening Reporting Center has seen a
95% success rate for over 7,000 juveniles. There has been several hundred participants in the Adult Drug
Program with over 50% success rate. These programs have been extremely cost effective and successfu l.
Finall y, he said the South Suburban Council on Alcoholism and Substance Abuse is one of the contracts
for the adult drug court program at District 6 in Markham and it has also been successful.
Commissioner Silvestri asked if there have been written reports on these programs which would indicate,
among other things, how many people have used the services since 1995 and 1998 respectively?
Mr. Anderson commented that Loyola University completed a study on programs at Di stricts 4 and 6 as
wel l as the Criminal Division Adult Court. He said that he will have the reports distributed to the
members of the Board.
Commissioner Sutker asked if these programs have been working with families as well as the juveniles
them selves?
Mr. Anderson responded in the affirmative.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked Mr. Anderson to provide this information to the Board prior to
presentation of their budget.

3262

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR SEPTEMBER 20, 200 I

Commissioner Butler stated that duplication is not an area of concern, and additional funds should be
al located and more programs should exist to expand these types of services in the county.
Commissioner Moran asked if there is a registration fee?
Mr. Anderson stated that the cost of the contracts before the Finance Committee today are paid by fees
collected from probationers. However he noted these programs used to be grant funded. With respect to
charging fees to juveniles, the biggest problem is most of the kids are poor and there is not enough
evidence to s upport that charging the kids would make a difference.
Commissioner Collins asked if the county receives third party reimbursement for providing drug
treatment?
Mr. Anderson answered in the affirmati ve and noted access to state Medicaid funding is available.
Chainnan Daley reiterated that the Sheriffs Office wi ll look at the programs and work together wi th the
Chief Judge's Office to provide reports to the County Board .
Undersheriff Whittler stated that a report was provided in March 200 I from a contract with HRDI
(Human Resources Development Institute) regardi ng the current program.
Commissioner Steele addressed the issue of coordinating these programs and maximizing their benefits.
She commented that the Bureau of Public Safety and Judic ia l Coordination was responsible for feedback
on the s uccess of the programs. The Commissioner noted that programs under the C hief Judge, Sheriff s
Office, State 's Attorney 's Office and the Judicial Advisory Council should be coordinated under one
office.
C ha irman Daley stated the report prepared by the University of Illinois (U. of I.) as Phase I, was
approved. The Chairman said the Board should consider the possibility of commissioning the University
of Illinois to complete Phase 2 to ascertain whether or not there is duplication of services, identify sources
o f funding, success ratio and recidivism.

Vice Chairman Carr, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved approval of Communication
Nos. 246131, 246132 as amended, 246133 as amended, 246134 as amended, 246135 and 246136. The
motion carried.
Commissioner Lechowicz moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Moreno. The
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.
Respectfully submitted,
COMMITTEE ON FINANCE
JOHN P. DALEY, Chairman
ATTEST: SANDRA K. WILLIAMS, Secretary

Finance be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON LAW ENFORCEMENT AND CORRECTIONS
May 23, 2001
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County
ATTENDANCE
Present

Chairman Moreno, Vice Chairman Silvestri, Commissioners Butler, Carr, Maldonado
and Quigley (6)

Absent:

Commissioner Schumann ( 1)

Also Present:

Michael Sheahan - Cook County Sheriff; Mr. Patrick Driscoll - Chief of the Civil Actions
Bureau, State's Attorney ' s Office; Judge Paul P. Biebel, Jr. - Presiding Judge, Cook
